###begin article-title 0
###xml 29 31 29 31 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 54 55 54 55 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 140 141 140 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn1">*</xref>
Modulation of Voltage- and Ca2+-dependent Gating of CaV1.3 L-type Calcium Channels by Alternative Splicing of a C-terminal Regulatory Domain*
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 98 126 98 126 <email xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">alexandra.koschak@uibk.ac.at</email>
 To whom correspondence should be addressed. Tel.: 43-512-507-5602; Fax: 42-512-507-2931; E-mail: alexandra.koschak@uibk.ac.at.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 0 15 0 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Author's Choice</italic>
Author's Choice
###end p 2
###begin p 3
 applies to Author Choice Articles
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 28 29 28 29 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 42 44 42 44 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 154 155 154 155 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 312 313 312 313 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 326 328 326 328 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 493 494 493 494 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 548 549 544 545 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 552 554 548 550 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 576 577 572 573 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 580 583 576 579 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 655 656 651 652 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 867 868 852 853 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 871 874 856 859 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 1033 1034 1018 1019 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1159 1160 1144 1145 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1163 1172 1148 1153 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C116</sub>
###xml 1220 1221 1201 1202 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1224 1227 1205 1208 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 1305 1308 1286 1289 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">116</sub>
###xml 1432 1433 1413 1414 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1589 1590 1570 1571 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1712 1713 1693 1694 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1774 1775 1755 1756 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
Low voltage activation of CaV1.3 L-type Ca2+ channels controls excitability in sensory cells and central neurons as well as sinoatrial node pacemaking. CaV1.3-mediated pacemaking determines neuronal vulnerability of dopaminergic striatal neurons affected in Parkinson disease. We have previously found that in CaV1.4 L-type Ca2+ channels, activation, voltage, and calcium-dependent inactivation are controlled by an intrinsic distal C-terminal modulator. Because alternative splicing in the CaV1.3 alpha1 subunit C terminus gives rise to a long (CaV1.342) and a short form (CaV1.342A), we investigated if a C-terminal modulatory mechanism also controls CaV1.3 gating. The biophysical properties of both splice variants were compared after heterologous expression together with beta3 and alpha2delta1 subunits in HEK-293 cells. Activation of calcium current through CaV1.342A channels was more pronounced at negative voltages, and inactivation was faster because of enhanced calcium-dependent inactivation. By investigating several CaV1.3 channel truncations, we restricted the modulator activity to the last 116 amino acids of the C terminus. The resulting CaV1.3DeltaC116 channels showed gating properties similar to CaV1.342A that were reverted by co-expression of the corresponding C-terminal peptide C116. Fluorescence resonance energy transfer experiments confirmed an intramolecular protein interaction in the C terminus of CaV1.3 channels that also modulates calmodulin binding. These experiments revealed a novel mechanism of channel modulation enabling cells to tightly control CaV1.3 channel activity by alternative splicing. The absence of the C-terminal modulator in short splice forms facilitates CaV1.3 channel activation at lower voltages expected to favor CaV1.3 activity at threshold voltages as required for modulation of neuronal firing behavior and sinoatrial node pacemaking.
###end p 4

###begin p 7
###xml 2 4 2 4 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 43 45 43 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 62 63 62 63 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn2">2</xref>
###xml 229 230 229 230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref1">1</xref>
###xml 278 279 274 275 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 285 286 281 282 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 378 380 374 376 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 410 411 406 407 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 572 573 568 569 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref2">2</xref>
###xml 578 579 574 575 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 837 838 833 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref3">3</xref>
###xml 839 840 835 836 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref5">5</xref>
###xml 865 866 861 862 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 883 884 879 880 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 954 955 950 951 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref7">7</xref>
###xml 957 958 953 954 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>
###xml 963 965 959 961 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1005 1007 1001 1003 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1090 1091 1086 1087 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref9">9</xref>
###xml 1168 1170 1164 1166 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1207 1209 1203 1205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref10">10</xref>
###xml 1211 1213 1207 1209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref11">11</xref>
###xml 1306 1307 1302 1303 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1352 1353 1348 1349 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1386 1387 1382 1383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1387 1389 1383 1385 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 1430 1431 1426 1427 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1523 1524 1519 1520 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1600 1602 1592 1594 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 1604 1606 1596 1598 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
###xml 1744 1746 1736 1738 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 1796 1797 1788 1789 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1852 1853 1844 1845 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1954 1956 1946 1948 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 1982 1983 1974 1975 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1999 2000 1991 1992 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 2050 2052 2038 2040 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref18">18</xref>
###xml 2053 2055 2041 2043 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref20">20</xref>
###xml 2162 2164 2150 2152 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 2166 2168 2154 2156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref21">21</xref>
Ca2+ influx through voltage-gated L-type Ca2+ channels (LTCCs)2 regulates numerous physiological functions, including muscle contraction, hormone release, neuronal firing and plasticity, sensory function, and cardiac pacemaking (1). Four pore-forming alpha1 subunit isoforms (CaV1.1-CaV1.4) with different biophysical properties and expression profiles evolved to adjust LTCC Ca2+ signals to cellular needs. CaV1.3 channels play a unique role for hearing (sensory signaling in cochlear inner hair cells (IHC)) and sinoatrial node (SAN, diastolic depolarization) function (2). CaV1.3 channels appear ideally suited for these functions because the operating range of both IHCs and SAN cells is within a voltage range of about -60 and -40 mV where these channels can conduct inward current because of their negative activation range (Refs. 3-5 and for review see Ref. 6). In neurons, CaV1.3 channels also serve pacemaker function and shape neuronal firing (7, 8). Ca2+ influx through LTCCs is limited by a Ca2+-dependent feedback mechanism, the so-called calcium-dependent inactivation (CDI) (9). CDI develops in response to local or global elevations of intracellular Ca2+ sensed by channel-bound calmodulin (10, 11). However, moderation of CDI is an important prerequisite in some cells, such as in IHCs (CaV1.3; 12-14) and in retinal photoreceptors (CaV1.4), where slow inactivation of ICa is required for sensory signaling. In CaV1.4 channels, CDI is completely prevented by an intrinsic gating modulator located in the CaV1.4alpha1 C terminus, and CDI is restored in C-terminal truncation mutants (15, 16). This C-terminal gating modulator (CTM) not only prevents CDI but also shifts the activation voltage range to more positive potentials (15). Gating modulation seems not to be limited to CaV1.4 because co-expression of C-terminal fragments of CaV1.2 channels also shifts their activation range to more positive voltages and inhibits pore opening (17). Because C termini of CaV1.2 (and also CaV1.1) alpha1 subunits are proteolytically cleaved (18-20) but remain noncovalently bound to proximal C-terminal domains, they may serve as autoinhibitory modules (17, 21).
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 23 24 23 24 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 89 90 89 90 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 97 98 97 98 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 109 110 109 110 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 187 188 183 184 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 239 240 231 232 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 243 245 235 237 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 278 279 270 271 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 282 285 274 277 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 365 366 357 358 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 401 405 393 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">i.e.</italic>
We hypothesized that CaV1.3 function may also be fine-tuned by a CTM domain similar to CaV1.1, CaV1.2, and CaV1.4. Unlike for other LTCC alpha1 subunits, alternative splicing generates CaV1.3 alpha1 subunits with long (usage of exon 42, CaV1.342) or short (usage of exon 42A, CaV1.342A) C termini. A CTM would therefore confer different biophysical properties on CaV1.3 only if present as in certain (i.e. long) variants.
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 143 144 143 144 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 147 149 147 149 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 156 157 156 157 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 160 163 160 163 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 334 335 334 335 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 246 251 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 256 261 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Here we provide unequivocal evidence that an intramolecular protein-protein interaction gives rise to substantial gating differences between CaV1.342 and CaV1.342A. Our finding that the long and the short splice variants are expressed in several mouse and human tissues suggests that both contribute to fine-tuning of physiological CaV1.3 channel function.
###end p 9

EXPERIMENTAL PROCEDURES

Cloning of cDNA Constructs

###begin p 12
###xml 29 30 29 30 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 33 36 33 36 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 95 96 95 96 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 108 109 108 109 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 112 114 112 114 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 125 126 125 126 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 129 131 129 131 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">8A</sub>
###xml 143 144 143 144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 358 359 336 337 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 405 406 383 384 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 504 505 482 483 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 569 570 547 548 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;</sup>
###xml 603 604 581 582 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 617 618 595 596 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 754 755 732 733 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 823 824 801 802 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 827 836 805 810 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C473</sub>
###xml 840 841 814 815 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 844 853 818 823 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 857 858 827 828 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 861 870 831 836 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C116</sub>
###xml 878 879 844 845 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 882 890 848 852 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C76</sub>
###xml 960 961 922 923 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 964 966 926 928 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 1095 1096 1057 1058 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1099 1108 1061 1066 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 1115 1116 1073 1074 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1119 1127 1077 1081 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C76</sub>
###xml 1141 1142 1095 1096 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1145 1154 1099 1104 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C116</sub>
###xml 1172 1173 1122 1123 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1176 1185 1126 1131 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C473</sub>
###xml 1201 1204 1147 1150 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">158</sub>
###xml 1211 1214 1157 1160 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">116</sub>
###xml 1225 1227 1171 1173 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">76</sub>
###xml 1363 1364 1309 1310 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1367 1369 1313 1315 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 1383 1384 1329 1330 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">+</sup>
###xml 1437 1438 1383 1384 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1463 1465 1409 1411 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref22">22</xref>
###xml 1504 1505 1450 1451 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1575 1583 1521 1529 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pEYFP-C1</italic>
###xml 1623 1631 1569 1577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pECFP-N1</italic>
###xml 1824 1825 1770 1771 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1906 1914 1852 1860 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pEYFP-C1</italic>
###xml 2096 2100 2042 2046 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RRQQ</sup>
###xml 2213 2216 2159 2162 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">158</sub>
###xml 2226 2229 2172 2175 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">116</sub>
###xml 2345 2346 2291 2292 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 2434 2442 2380 2388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pECFP-N1</italic>
###xml 2470 2473 2416 2419 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">116</sub>
###xml 2473 2477 2419 2423 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">DEQQ</sup>
###xml 2707 2708 2653 2654 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 2711 2713 2657 2659 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 117 122 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 264 267 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 426 429 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 479 484 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 496 501 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Human</span>
To generate splice variant CaV1.342A, the alternatively spliced exon 42A was introduced into CaV1.3 cDNA (CaV1.342 = human CaV1.38A as in Ref. 4, GenBanktrade mark accession number EU363339) by co-ligating an EcoRI-BamHI-cut PCR product containing exon 42A from a rat brain alpha1 subunit (GenBanktrade mark accession number M57682) with HindIII-EcoRI-cut CaV1.3 cDNA into HindIII-BamHI (4622-7100)-cut CaV1.3-pBS vector. The rat exon 42A amino acid sequence is identical to its human homologue. Human CaV1.3 containing exon 42A was subsequently cloned into vector pGFP- (wild type) short form of the CaV1.3 protein (4). For analyzing the effects of exon 44, amino acid residues RTRYYETYI were introduced into an untagged construct containing the long CaV1.3 C terminus after position 1787 using standard PCR techniques. CaV1.3DeltaC473, CaV1.3DeltaC158, CaV1.3DeltaC116, and CaV1.3DeltaC76 channels were constructed by introducing stop codons into untagged CaV1.342 at respective amino acid positions 1665, 1980, 2022, and 2062 followed by artificial restriction sites as follows: BamHI* for CaV1.3DeltaC158 and CaV1.3DeltaC76, HpaI* for CaV1.3DeltaC116, and XhoI* for CaV1.3DeltaC473. Peptides GFP-C158, GFP-C116, and GFP-C76 were constructed by ligating HindIII*-SalI*-flanked PCR products corresponding to amino acids 1980-2137, 2022-2137, and 2062-2137 of CaV1.342 into the pGFP+ plasmid resulting in the corresponding GFP-tagged CaV1.3 C-terminal peptides (22). For FRET analysis, all C-terminal CaV1.3 fragments were cloned either into the mammalian expression vector pEYFP-C1 for N-terminal EYFP labeling or vector pECFP-N1 for C-terminal enhanced CFP labeling (Clontech). N-terminally EYFP-labeled constructs 5'-HindIII* and 3'-SalI* restriction sites flanking nucleotide sequences corresponding to the following CaV1.3 amino acid positions were introduced and cloned into HindIII-SalI-cut vector pEYFP-C1 as follows: peptide EF-preIQ-IQ-postIQ, amino acids 1453-2137; EF-preIQ-IQ, amino acids 1453-1623; and EF-preIQ-IQ-PCRD, amino acids 1453-1664. To construct peptide EF-preIQ-IQ-PCRDRRQQ, arginines at positions 1640 and 1641 were mutated to glutamines by splicing by overlapping extension-PCR. For C158-CFP and C116-CFP, 5'-EcoRI* and 3'-BamHI* restriction sites were introduced to flanking nucleotide sequences corresponding to CaV1.3 amino acid positions 1980-2137 and 2022-2137 and cloned into EcoRI-BamHI-cut vector pECFP-N1. To generate enhanced CFP-C116DEQQ, aspartate and glutamate at positions 2073 and 2076 were mutated to glutamines by splicing by overlapping extension-PCR. Integrity of all constructs was confirmed by DNA sequencing (MWG Biotec, Martinsried, Germany). Construct CaV1.342 was subjected to full-length sequence analysis. Numbering of amino acids or nucleotide positions in all constructs refers to GenBanktrade mark accession number EU363339. Asterisks indicate artificial restriction sites introduced by PCR.
###end p 12
###begin title 13
Qualitative RT-PCR
###end title 13
###begin p 14
###xml 376 378 374 376 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref23">23</xref>
###xml 852 853 831 832 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 856 858 835 837 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 865 866 844 845 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 869 872 848 851 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 2542 2543 2463 2464 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 2548 2549 2469 2470 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 49 53 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 350 354 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 380 385 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Human</span>
###xml 794 799 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 817 822 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 990 995 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1214 1219 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1401 1406 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1693 1698 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 1703 1708 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1760 1765 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1914 1919 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Mouse tissue was prepared from C57B/6N wild-type mice. Total RNA was isolated from whole-brain and brain sub-regions using the RNAqueos(R)-4PCR kit (Ambion, Foster City, CA). After DNase I treatment, RNA integrity was checked by the quality of the 28 S and 18 S rRNA bands on a denaturing agarose gel. Organ of Corti mRNA was prepared from P4 or P19 mice as described in Ref. 23. Human total RNAs from brain, heart, pancreas, and retina were purchased from Clontech. One mug of total RNA was used for first strand cDNA synthesis by reverse transcriptase (RevertAidtrade mark H Minus First Strand cDNA synthesis kit, MBI; Fermentas, Hanover, Germany) and random hexamer primers. For PCR analysis, the forward (fwd) primer was located in exon 39 (GenBanktrade mark accession number NM_028981 for mouse and EU363339 for human). To differentiate between CaV1.342 and CaV1.342A, specific reverse (rev) primers were designed, located either in exon 42 or 42A. The following primers were used for mouse: fwd primer, 5'-CAACCCTGTTTGCTTTGGTC-3', and rev primer for exon 42, 5'TATAGCCCGTCGGATTTCTG-3' (332-bp product); rev primer for exon 42A, 5'-CTTCCTTCCGGAGGAGTGC-3' (483-bp product). The following primers were used for human: fwd primer, 5'-AACCCTGTTTGCTTTGGTTC-3', rev primer for exon 42, 5'-TATAGCACGCCGGATTTCTG-3' (331-bp product); rev primer for exon 42A, 5'-CCACCTTCCGGAGGAGTG-3' (488-bp product). In mouse organ of Corti, splice variants were also detected with the following primer pairs: exon 42 fwd primer, 5'-CTGCTTGACCAAGTTGTCCCTCCA-3', rev primer, 5'-CTACAAGGTGGTAATGCAAATCAT-3'; exon 42A, fwd primer, 5'-CGCGGATCCTACTTGACCAAGTTGTCCC-3'; rev primer, 5'-CGCAAGCTTCTAGAGCATCCGTTCAAGC-3'. Mouse and human GAPDH was used as positive control as follows: for mouse (GenBanktrade mark accession number NM_008084), fwd primer, 5'-ACTCCACTCACGGCAAATTC-3', rev primer 5'-CACATTGGGGGTAGGAACAC-3' (572-bp product); for human (GenBanktrade mark accession number NM_002046), fwd primer, CAATGACCCCTTCATTGACC, rev primer, 5'-GAGGCAGGGATGATGTTCTG-3' (531-bp product). 500 ng (2.7 mug for organ of Corti) of reverse-transcribed cDNA was used as template for each PCR. Samples without template were used as contamination control. The following PCR program was used: 94 degreesC for 3 min, 40 cycles of 94 degreesC for 45 s, 55 degreesC for 45 s, and 68 degreesC for 1 min, followed by an elongation step of 68 degreesC for 10 min. PCRs were performed using BioThermtrade mark TaqDNA polymerase (GeneCraft, Ludinghausen, Germany) in the presence of 1.5 mm MgCl2. The resulting PCR products were subcloned into pGEM-T Easy vectors (Promega, Mannheim, Germany) and sequenced.
###end p 14
###begin title 15
Quantitative RT-PCR
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 0 34 0 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RNA Isolation and cDNA Preparation</italic>
###xml 203 205 203 205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref24">24</xref>
###xml 73 77 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
RNA Isolation and cDNA Preparation-Tissue from three adult male c57BL/6N mice (3-6 months) was used for whole-brain and brain sub-region cDNA preparations. Total RNA and cDNA were prepared as described (24).
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Quantitative RT-PCR</italic>
###xml 58 59 58 59 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 165 167 165 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref24">24</xref>
###xml 454 455 454 455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E</italic>
###xml 478 479 478 479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E</italic>
###xml 312 317 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Quantitative RT-PCR-The relative abundance of different CaV1.3 mRNAs was assessed by TaqMan quantitative PCR (50 cycles) using a standard curve method as described (24). TaqMan gene expression assays, designed to span exon-exon boundaries, were purchased from Applied Biosystems (Foster City, CA). Assessment of mouse GAPDH transcripts was included as efficiency reference. Assay identification numbers are as follows: exon 42, Mm0551393_m1 (efficiency (E) = 103.6%); exon 42A (E = 98.7%), custom-designed (fwd primer, 5'-GGAAGTACCCTGCGAAGAACAC-3'; probe, 5'-TTGCCCTACAGATGCTTG-3'; rev primer, 5'-CTCAGGCAGAGAACTCTAAAGCAT-3'); GAPDH, Mm99999915_g1. To amplify specific cDNA templates from the analyzed tissues for the standard curves of each assay, primer pairs were as follows: exon 42 fwd primer, 5'-CAACCCTGTTTGCTTTGGTC-3', rev primer, 5'-TGATTGACATGGTTTCCAAGC-3'; exon 42A fwd primer, 5'-CAACCCTGTTTGCTTTGGTC-3', rev primer, 5'-CTTCCTTCCGGAGGAGTGC-3'. Analysis was carried out in triplicate.
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 0 37 0 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Cell Culture and Transient Expression</italic>
###xml 117 118 117 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 132 133 132 133 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 210 211 196 197 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 229 230 211 212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
###xml 284 285 266 267 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 448 450 430 432 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref25">25</xref>
###xml 532 533 510 511 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref4">4</xref>
Cell Culture and Transient Expression-HEK-293 (tsA-201) cells were cultured and transfected as described previously (4). Untagged CaV1.3alpha1 constructs were expressed together with beta3 (or beta2a) and alpha2delta 1 subunits (4). In co-expression studies, GFP-labeled C-terminal CaV1.3 fragments were used to ensure the presence of the corresponding C-terminal peptide in the cell recorded. Immunoblotting was performed as described previously (25) using a generic anti-alpha1 sequence-directed antibody as described previously (4). All constructs were expressed with the expected molecular mass.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 0 31 0 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Electrophysiological Recordings</italic>
###xml 177 178 177 178 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>

###xml 284 285 284 285 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 340 341 340 341 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>

###xml 405 406 405 406 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 444 445 444 445 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 484 485 484 485 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>

###xml 835 838 835 838 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">max</sub>
###xml 839 840 839 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 843 844 843 844 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 844 847 844 847 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rev</sub>
###xml 859 860 859 860 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 863 864 863 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 864 870 864 870 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">0.5act</sub>
###xml 872 873 872 873 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 883 884 883 884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 884 887 884 887 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rev</sub>
###xml 928 929 928 929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 953 954 953 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 986 987 986 987 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G</italic>
###xml 987 990 987 990 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">max</sub>
###xml 1025 1026 1025 1026 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 1026 1033 1026 1033 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">0.5,act</sub>
###xml 1078 1079 1078 1079 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 1261 1262 1261 1262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 1262 1265 1262 1265 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">max</sub>
###xml 1274 1277 1274 1277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I&#8211;V</italic>
###xml 1403 1404 1403 1404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 1404 1407 1404 1407 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">max</sub>
###xml 1568 1569 1568 1569 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1573 1575 1573 1575 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">SS</sub>
###xml 1572 1575 1572 1575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I<sub>SS</sub></italic>
###xml 1584 1586 1584 1586 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">SS</sub>
###xml 1583 1586 1583 1586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I<sub>SS</sub></italic>
###xml 1597 1598 1597 1598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 1601 1602 1601 1602 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 1602 1611 1602 1611 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">0.5,inact</sub>
###xml 1612 1613 1612 1613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 1613 1618 1613 1618 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">inact</sub>
###xml 1628 1629 1628 1629 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1662 1664 1662 1664 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">SS</sub>
###xml 1661 1664 1661 1664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I<sub>SS</sub></italic>
###xml 1698 1699 1698 1699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 1727 1728 1727 1728 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 1728 1737 1728 1737 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">0.5,inact</sub>
###xml 1778 1779 1778 1779 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 1779 1784 1779 1784 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">inact</sub>
###xml 1823 1824 1823 1824 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1827 1829 1827 1829 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 1836 1837 1836 1837 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1840 1843 1840 1843 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 2271 2272 2271 2272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">r</italic>
###xml 2272 2275 2272 2275 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">250</sub>
###xml 2288 2289 2288 2289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">f</italic>
###xml 2328 2329 2328 2329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">r</italic>
###xml 2329 2332 2329 2332 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">250</sub>
###xml 2343 2344 2343 2344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 2344 2346 2344 2346 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 2351 2352 2351 2352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 2352 2354 2352 2354 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 2487 2489 2487 2489 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 2495 2497 2495 2497 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
Electrophysiological Recordings-Whole-cell patch clamp recordings in transiently transfected HEK-293 (tsA-201) cells were performed 2-3 days after transfection using either 15 mm Ba2+ or Ca2+ as charge carrier as described in Ref. 4. Recording solutions were composed as follows (in mm): intracellular solution, 135 CsCl, 10 Cs-EGTA, 1 MgCl2 adjusted to pH 7.4 with CsOH (311 mosm); bath solution, 15 BaCl2, 10 HEPES, 150 choline-Cl, and 1 MgCl2, adjusted to pH 7.4 with CsOH (358 mosm). Transfected cells were visualized by co-expression of GFP or GFP- or YFP-labeled constructs co-expressed with the channel complex as indicated. Current-voltage (I-V) relationships were obtained by holding cells at a potential of -90 mV before applying 50-ms or 300-ms pulses to various test potentials. I-V curves were fitted to the equation I = Gmax(V - Vrev)/{1 + exp((V - V0.5act)/k)}, where Vrev is the extrapolated reversal potential; V is the test potential; I is the peak current amplitude; Gmax is the maximum slope conductance; V0.5,act is the half-maximal activation voltage; and k is the slope factor. Percentage of inactivation was determined at specified time points during depolarizing pulses from a holding potential of -90 mV to the peak current potential (Vmax) of the I-V relation of the individual cell. The voltage dependence of inactivation was assessed by application of a 20-ms test pulse to Vmax before and after holding cells at various conditioning test potentials for 5 s. Steady-state inactivation curves were analyzed using the Boltzmann relationship I = ISS + (1 - ISS)/(1 + exp(V - V0.5,inact/kinact)), where I is the peak current amplitude; ISS is the noninactivating fraction; V is the membrane potential; V0.5,inact is the half-inactivation potential; and kinact is the slope factor. To investigate CaV1.342 and CaV1.342A gating properties, head-to-head analysis was performed time-independently by two investigators. Experiments showing currents bigger than 3 nA were prospectively excluded from analysis of activation and inactivation parameters to guarantee high quality voltage clamp. CDI was quantified as the current remaining at the end of 250-ms depolarizations to different test potentials, expressed as fraction of peak current amplitude (r250). Parameter f was defined as the difference between r250 values of IBa and ICa at +10 mV. CDI experiments were performed on different cells, but effects were the same when the charge carrier was switched from Ba2+ to Ca2+ on the same cell in representative experiments. All voltages were corrected for the liquid junction potential.
###end p 19
###begin title 20
Confocal FRET Microscopy
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 64 66 64 66 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 99 102 99 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">YFP</italic>
###xml 178 181 178 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CFP</italic>
###xml 183 186 183 186 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">158</sub>
###xml 190 193 190 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CFP</italic>
###xml 195 198 195 198 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">116</sub>
###xml 366 368 366 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref26">26</xref>
Confocal FRET microscopy was performed as described previously (15). As negative controls, peptide YFP-EF-PreIQ-IQ-PCRD was co-expressed with CFP alone (CFP control), and probes CFP-C158 or CFP-C116 with YFP alone (YFP controls 1 and 2). Image analysis was accomplished using a self-made program integrated in MatLab 7 based on the FRET analysis algorithm proposed (26). Interaction between fragments was considered when a significant difference to the CFP as well as the corresponding YFP control was observed. The local ratio between CFP and YFP might vary because of different local expression levels of the different protein constructs, which could affect calculation of FRET values. Therefore, analysis was limited to pixels with a CFP:YFP molar ratio between 1:10 and 10:1.
###end p 21
###begin title 22
Statistical Analysis
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 191 199 187 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a priori</italic>
###xml 320 321 316 317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">t</italic>
###xml 603 604 599 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
Data were analyzed using Clampfit(R) 9.0 (Molecular Devices, Union City, CA) and Microcal Origin(R) 5.0 (Northampton, MA). Significant difference between the two splice variants was assessed a priori by pairwise comparison before other truncation constructs to characterize the modulatory mechanism were made. Student's t test or Mann-Whitney test were used for comparison between two groups for parametric and nonparametric data, respectively. Statistical significance was determined using one-way ANOVA followed by Bonferroni post-test, except if stated otherwise. Statistical significance was set at p < 0.05. All data are presented as mean +/- S.E. for the indicated number of experiments.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
RESULTS
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 2 3 2 3 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 0 70 0 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca<sub>V</sub>1.3 C-terminal Modulator Affects Voltage-dependent Channel Activity</italic>
###xml 188 189 188 189 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 227 228 223 224 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 231 233 227 229 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 240 241 236 237 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 244 247 240 243 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 263 264 259 260 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 275 276 271 272 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 296 297 292 293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref5">5</xref>
###xml 299 301 295 297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref27">27</xref>
###xml 303 305 299 301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref28">28</xref>
###xml 393 394 389 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</italic>
###xml 387 394 383 390 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1<italic>a</italic></xref>
###xml 413 414 409 410 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 441 442 437 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">X</italic>
###xml 444 446 440 442 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 451 452 447 448 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 455 458 451 454 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 632 633 628 629 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 638 640 634 636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 670 671 666 667 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 917 919 892 894 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref29">29</xref>
###xml 1038 1039 1009 1010 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">b</italic>
###xml 1032 1039 1003 1010 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1<italic>b</italic></xref>
CaV1.3 C-terminal Modulator Affects Voltage-dependent Channel Activity-To test for the presence of a C-terminal modulator (CTM), we employed two previously described naturally occurring CaV1.3 alpha1 subunit splice variants, CaV1.342 and CaV1.342A (also termed CaV1.3a and CaV1.3b, respectively (5, 27, 28)), which differ with respect to the length of their C termini, as illustrated in Fig. 1a. Similar to the CaV1.4 truncation mutant K1591X (15), CaV1.342A terminates shortly after the IQ motif and lacks most of a homologous region (termed PCRD) previously found to participate in the binding of distal C-terminal sequences in CaV1.2 (17). Wild-type long and short CaV1.3 alpha1 subunits were expressed in HEK-293 cells together with beta3 (or beta2a) and alpha2delta 1. beta3 subunits were selected because we have previously shown that they form a large fraction of dihydropyridine-sensitive LTCCs in the brain (29). Both alpha1 subunits migrated with the expected molecular mass in Western blots of HEK-293 cell preparations (Fig. 1b).
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 0 9 0 9 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FIGURE 1.</label>
###xml 38 39 38 39 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 42 44 42 44 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 51 52 51 52 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>

###xml 1096 1098 1078 1080 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 1118 1119 1098 1099 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>

###xml 1192 1195 1170 1173 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 1242 1243 1208 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1243 1245 1209 1211 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 1249 1250 1215 1216 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1253 1255 1219 1221 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 1277 1278 1241 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1287 1288 1251 1252 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1291 1294 1255 1258 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 1311 1312 1273 1274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1319 1320 1281 1282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 1385 1386 1347 1348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1386 1388 1348 1350 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 1524 1525 1486 1487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">b</italic>
###xml 1518 1525 1480 1487 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1<italic>b</italic></xref>
###xml 1525 1528 1487 1490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, n</italic>
###xml 1577 1578 1539 1540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 1578 1581 1540 1543 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rev</sub>
###xml 1652 1653 1614 1615 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1656 1658 1618 1620 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 1706 1707 1668 1669 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1710 1713 1672 1675 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 1730 1731 1692 1693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</italic>
###xml 1724 1731 1686 1693 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>d</italic></xref>
###xml 1795 1796 1757 1758 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1799 1802 1761 1764 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
We systematically investigated the biophysical properties of both ICa and IBa for CaV1.342 and CaV1.342A as illustrated in Figs. 2 and 3 and Tables 1, 2, 3. The voltage dependence of ICa activation of CaV1.342A was significantly shifted to hyperpolarizing potentials by about 10 mV (CaV1.342: V0.5,act = -2.2 +/- 0.6 mV, n = 14; CaV1.342A: V0.5,act = -12.9 +/- 0.8 mV, n = 15; p < 0.001; see Table 1). This negative shift was because of the significant decrease in kact (CaV1.342: -9.1 +/- 0.2, n = 14; CaV1.342A: -6.9 +/- 0.2, n = 15; p < 0.001; see Table 1) without change in the activation threshold (Fig. 2a). Such changes were also observed for IBa (Table 2). The negative activation range persisted when subgroups of cells with different current amplitudes (0.1-0.6 versus 0.7-2.3 nA) were compared (Fig. 2c). It was not restricted to beta3 subunit-containing channel complexes because it was also seen when the CaV1.3 splice variants were co-expressed with beta2a subunits (V0.5,act, ICa, CaV1.342, V0.5,act, 0.06 +/- 3.2 mV, n = 3, CaV1.342A, V0.5,act, -11.2 +/- 1.7 mV,n = 3; IBa, CaV1.342, -12.5 +/- 1.6 mV, n = 7, CaV1.342A, -22.7 +/- 1.3 mV, n = 6). Mean current density of CaV1.342A channels was approximately2.5-fold higher for ICa (CaV1.342, 21.0 +/- 3.3 pA/pF, n = 14; CaV1.342A, 98.3 +/- 31.8, n = 19, p < 0.01, Mann-Whitney test). A similar increase was observed for IBa (not shown). Increased current density occurred without detectable changes in the expression density as observed in immunoblots (Fig. 1b, n = 4). Depolarization to the reversal potential (Vrev) revealed a small ON-gating current which was always detectable for CaV1.342 channels but was absent (or much reduced) in CaV1.342A currents (Fig. 2d). This further suggests that the larger current amplitude of CaV1.342A channels was not because of an increased expression density of channels at the plasma membrane in line with the immunoblot analysis.
###end p 30

###begin p 52
###xml 59 60 59 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 60 63 60 63 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rev</sub>
###xml 126 127 126 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 127 129 127 129 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 142 143 142 143 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">1</xref>
###xml 148 149 148 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">2</xref>
###xml 207 208 207 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 208 215 208 215 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">0.5,act</sub>
###xml 260 261 260 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e</italic>
###xml 254 261 254 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>e</italic></xref>
###xml 366 367 366 367 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 370 373 370 373 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 386 387 386 387 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 390 392 390 392 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 412 413 410 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 421 422 419 420 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 425 428 423 426 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 448 449 444 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 455 456 451 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 476 477 472 473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">t</italic>
###xml 531 532 527 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 532 537 528 533 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">inact</sub>
###xml 541 542 537 538 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 545 547 541 543 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 566 567 560 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 575 576 569 570 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 579 582 573 576 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 601 602 593 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 608 609 600 601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 628 629 620 621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">t</italic>
###xml 825 826 817 818 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 829 832 821 824 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 840 841 832 833 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e</italic>
###xml 834 841 826 833 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>e</italic></xref>
###xml 928 929 920 921 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1032 1033 1024 1025 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
The short C terminus also resulted in a slight decrease of Vrev (with a larger and statistically significantly difference for IBa; see Tables 1 and 2). The half-maximal voltage of steady-state inactivation (V0.5,act) induced by 10-s conditioning pulses (Fig. 2e) for the physiological charge carrier was also significantly shifted toward more negative voltages in CaV1.342A channels (CaV1.342: -31.6 +/- 1.1 mV, n = 5; CaV1.342A: -38.8 +/- 1.6 mV, n = 4, p = 0.007, Student's t test). A significant difference in the slope factor (kinact, CaV1.342: -6.4 +/- 0.3 mV, n = 5; CaV1.342A: -4.9 +/- 0.5 mV, n = 4, p = 0.03, Student's t test) was also observed. Theses changes in the voltage dependence of steady-state activation and inactivation resulted in a shift of the window current toward more hyperpolarizing voltages for CaV1.342A (Fig. 2e). Our data demonstrate that the structural divergence within the C termini of these CaV1.3 splice variants causes pronounced changes in channel gating suggesting the existence of a CTM in CaV1.3 LTCCs that controls their activity at negative voltages.
###end p 52

###xml 919 921 911 913 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 939 940 931 932 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1027 1028 1019 1020 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1028 1030 1020 1022 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 1049 1050 1041 1042 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1053 1056 1045 1048 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 1169 1170 1161 1162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1170 1172 1162 1164 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 1206 1207 1198 1199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">c</italic>
###xml 1200 1207 1192 1199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>c</italic></xref>
###xml 1361 1362 1341 1342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref5">5</xref>
###xml 1430 1432 1410 1412 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
CaV1.3 C Terminus Modulates Ca2+-dependent Inactivation Properties-As already obvious from the representative current traces in Fig. 2b, CaV1.342A channels inactivate faster during depolarization to different test potentials than CaV1.342 channels. This is also evident from a detailed comparison of ICa inactivation during 10-s pulses to the maximum of the I-V curve (Vmax) (Fig. 3, a and b; Table 3). The difference was most pronounced during the first 30 ms (% inactivation: CaV1.342, 27.5 +/- 1.9, n = 16; CaV1.342A, 73.6 +/- 1.9, n = 19, p < 0.001; Fig. 3, a, inset, and b, and Table 3). Inactivation included an initial fast component followed by a slow component in both isoforms. Inactivation was not complete even during 10 s (CaV1.342, 96.9 +/- 0.7%, n = 14; CaV1.342A, 98.1 +/- 0.3%, n = 17; one sample t test, compared with 100%: p = 0.0006 for CaV1.342 and p = 0.0001 for CaV1.342A) suggesting that some Ca2+ influx through CaV1.3 channels may persist even during extended periods of strong depolarization. Faster ICa inactivation of CaV1.342A was also seen at physiologically more relevant potentials, as indicated by a significant decrease in integrated ICa during 300-ms test pulses (Fig. 3c). Note that voltage dependence of activation and inactivation is shifted by approximately15 mV to more positive voltages under our recording conditions (5). Therefore, -20 mV corresponds to about -35 mV at physiological Ca2+ concentrations.
###end p 53

###xml 929 930 913 914 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">t</italic>

###end p 55
###begin p 56
###xml 29 30 29 30 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 33 36 33 36 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 160 161 160 161 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 174 175 174 175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 175 177 175 177 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 223 224 223 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 224 226 224 226 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 262 263 262 263 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 266 269 266 269 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 286 287 286 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</italic>
###xml 280 287 280 287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>d</italic></xref>
###xml 292 299 292 299 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 411 412 411 412 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 415 418 415 418 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 448 449 446 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 537 538 535 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 538 540 536 538 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 556 557 554 555 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 571 573 569 571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
The faster inactivation of CaV1.342A could be due to faster voltage-dependent inactivation, faster CDI, or both. To address this question, we also quantified CaV1.3-mediated IBa of both splice variants. Interestingly, mean IBa inactivation was even slower for CaV1.342A channels (Fig. 3d and Table 3). This difference was because of a pronounced slowing of inactivation in 50% of the cells (% inactivation of CaV1.342A during 250 ms, 8.6 +/- 1.2%, n = 7, in this subset). We have previously observed a similar slowing of inactivation of IBa in truncated CaV1.4 channels (15).
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 60 61 60 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 61 63 61 63 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 79 80 79 80 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 83 86 83 86 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 185 186 185 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 186 188 186 188 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 199 200 199 200 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 254 255 254 255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">r</italic>
###xml 255 258 255 258 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">250</sub>
###xml 291 292 291 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e</italic>
###xml 285 292 285 292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>e</italic></xref>
###xml 413 414 413 414 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 417 420 417 420 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 431 432 431 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">f</italic>
###xml 449 455 447 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">versus</italic>
###xml 485 486 481 482 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 489 491 485 487 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 540 542 536 538 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref13">13</xref>
###xml 547 548 543 544 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 574 575 570 571 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 575 577 571 573 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 596 597 592 593 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 600 603 596 599 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 695 699 691 695 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1234</sub>
###xml 702 703 698 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">r</italic>
###xml 703 706 699 702 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">250</sub>
###xml 710 711 706 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 711 714 707 710 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">max</sub>
###xml 717 718 713 714 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 721 724 717 720 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 730 734 726 730 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1234</sub>
###xml 753 754 747 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 760 761 754 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 782 783 776 777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">t</italic>
###xml 789 795 783 789 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">versus</italic>
###xml 798 799 792 793 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 802 805 796 799 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 824 825 818 819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">r</italic>
###xml 825 828 819 822 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">250</sub>
###xml 840 841 834 835 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 841 843 835 837 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 870 871 864 865 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e</italic>
###xml 864 871 858 865 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>e</italic></xref>
###xml 877 881 871 875 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1234</sub>
###xml 930 931 924 925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 931 933 925 927 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 946 947 940 941 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 947 954 941 948 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">0.5,act</sub>
###xml 957 958 951 952 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 961 964 955 958 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 970 974 964 968 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1234</sub>
###xml 994 995 986 987 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1106 1107 1098 1099 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1112 1114 1104 1106 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 1191 1192 1183 1184 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
From these data we conclude that the faster inactivation of ICa observed for CaV1.342A must be due to more pronounced CDI. As a quantitative measure of CDI, we analyzed the fraction of ICa through CaV1.3 channels remaining after a 250-ms depolarization (r250) in a wide voltage range (Fig. 3e). A typical U-shaped dependence on test voltage was observed for both splice variants, but it was more pronounced for CaV1.342A channels (f = 0.60 +/- 0.07 versus 0.25 +/- 0.11 at 10 mV for CaV1.342 channels). In agreement with a previous report (13), CaV1.3 CDI was CaM-mediated. ICa inactivation of CaV1.342A channels was dramatically slowed by co-expression of YFP-labeled dominant-negative CaM (CaM1234) (r250 at Vmax:CaV1.342A + CaM1234, 0.76 +/- 0.061%, n = 5, p < 0.0001, Student's t test versus CaV1.342A) thus approaching r250 values for IBa (for comparison see Fig. 3e). CaM1234 did not affect the hyperpolarizing shift of the ICa activation (V0.5,act:CaV1.342A + CaM1234: -16.3 +/- 0.5 mV, n = 8) suggesting that the shift in activation voltage occurs independent of CaM as also shown previously for CaV1.4 (15). Taken together, these data provide unequivocal evidence that the CTM in CaV1.3 channels not only modulates its activity range but also moderates CDI.
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 2 3 2 3 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 0 82 0 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca<sub>V</sub>1.3 CTM Lies within the Most Distal C-terminal Domain Highly Conserved in LTCCs</italic>
###xml 283 286 283 286 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">122</sub>
###xml 303 304 303 304 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 328 330 328 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 390 391 390 391 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 394 396 394 396 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 414 415 414 415 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 418 427 418 423 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 447 448 443 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 448 450 444 446 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 455 456 451 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 456 458 452 454 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 499 500 495 496 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 503 506 499 502 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 515 516 511 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">1</xref>
###xml 521 522 517 518 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">2</xref>
###xml 529 530 525 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 530 532 526 528 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 534 535 530 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 535 538 531 534 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">act</sub>
###xml 566 567 562 563 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 570 579 566 571 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 595 596 585 586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 602 603 592 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 613 620 603 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 627 628 617 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 628 635 618 625 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">0.5,act</sub>
###xml 639 640 629 630 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 643 652 633 638 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 672 673 656 657 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 679 680 663 664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 690 697 674 681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 750 751 734 735 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 754 757 738 741 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 759 760 743 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 760 762 744 746 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 821 822 805 806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 822 824 806 808 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 876 877 860 861 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">1</xref>
###xml 879 880 863 864 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">2</xref>
###xml 882 883 866 867 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl3">3</xref>
CaV1.3 CTM Lies within the Most Distal C-terminal Domain Highly Conserved in LTCCs-To further strengthen this hypothesis and pinpoint important structural domains, we tested if different C-terminal truncations exhibit similar gating effects. In accordance to the C-terminal peptide C122 important for CaV1.4 channel modulation (15), we deleted the corresponding distal 158 amino acids of CaV1.342. The resulting CaV1.3DeltaC158 channels exhibited ICa and IBa activation properties comparable with CaV1.342A (Tables 1 and 2). For ICa, kact significantly decreased (CaV1.3DeltaC158: -7.4 +/- 0.2, n = 9; p < 0.001; Table 1), and V0.5,act (CaV1.3DeltaC158: -14.3 +/- 0.4 mV, n = 9, p < 0.001; Table 1) shifted to more hyperpolarized voltages. Like in CaV1.342A, ICa inactivation was faster, and CDI was more pronounced, and IBa was slowed (for all data and statistics see Tables 1, 2, 3).
###end p 58
###begin p 59
###xml 211 214 211 214 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">158</sub>
###xml 283 286 283 286 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">158</sub>
###xml 329 330 329 330 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 333 342 333 338 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 375 376 371 372 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 379 381 375 377 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 416 417 412 413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 417 419 413 415 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 451 452 447 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 452 456 448 452 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">0.5,</sub>
###xml 456 459 452 455 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">act</sub>
###xml 462 463 458 459 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 466 475 462 467 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 483 486 475 478 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">158</sub>
###xml 504 505 494 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 511 512 501 502 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 519 525 509 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">versus</italic>
###xml 528 529 518 519 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 532 534 522 524 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 540 547 530 537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 550 551 540 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 551 553 541 543 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 595 596 585 586 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 599 608 589 594 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 616 619 602 605 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">158</sub>
###xml 636 637 620 621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 643 644 627 628 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 651 657 635 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">versus</italic>
###xml 660 661 644 645 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 664 666 648 650 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 672 679 656 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 746 747 730 731 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">f</italic>
###xml 767 768 751 752 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 771 780 755 760 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 788 791 768 771 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">158</sub>
###xml 807 808 785 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 820 827 798 805 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl3">Table 3</xref>
###xml 918 919 896 897 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 919 921 897 899 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 923 930 901 908 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">Table 2</xref>
To prove the modulatory role of the last 158 amino acid residues, we tested the capability of this C-terminal fragment to restore the gating changes induced by the truncation. Therefore, GFP-fused peptide (GFP-C158) was expressed together with the respective truncated channel. GFP-C158 reverted the gating changes observed in CaV1.3DeltaC158 channels to values similar to CaV1.342; the hyperpolarizing shift of the ICa activation curve was reversed (V0.5,act:CaV1.3DeltaC158 + GFP-C158, -0.8 +/- 1.4 mV n = 8, p = 0.3 versus CaV1.342; see Table 1); ICa inactivation was slowed (during 30 ms: CaV1.3DeltaC158 + GFP-C158; 23.5 +/- 1.9%, n = 8, p = 0.2 versus CaV1.342; see Table 3), and CDI was less pronounced as indicated by the decrease of the f value (at 10 mV, CaV1.3DeltaC158 + GFP-C158, 0.2 +/- 0.08, n = 6-8; see Table 3). Peptide-induced reversal of activation and inactivation parameters was also observed in IBa (Table 2).

FIGURE 4.Gating properties of CaV1.3DeltaC116 channels and effect of the distal CTM peptide C116. Data for CaV1.342 were taken from Fig. 2. a, representative normalized I-V curves for ICa. Activation parameters were as follows (in mV): CaV1.342: V0.5,act, -4.2, and kact, -8.6; CaV1.3DeltaC116: V0.5,act: -12.8, and kact, -7.7; CaV1.3DeltaC116+GFP-C116: V0.5,act, -4.7, and kact, -8.8; Cells: 196l_23, 27g_57, and 27g_91, respectively. b, representative current traces of ICa evoked by a depolarization to Vmax. Cells: CaV1.3DeltaC116, 27g_27; CaV1.3DeltaC116+GFP-C116, 197f_26. c, percent ICa inactivation during test pulses to Vmax: **, p < 0.01; ***, p < 0.001, compared with CaV1.342 (black); +, p < 0.05; +++, p < 0.001, comparison of CaV1.3DeltaC116 + GFP-C116 (white) with CaV1.3DeltaC116 (gray) alone (one-way ANOVA followed by Bonferroni post-test). Number of experiments is given in parentheses. Error bars reflect S.E. d and e, representative ICa traces for CaV1.3DeltaC116 (d) and CaV1.3DeltaC116+GFP-C116 (e). Cells: 27g_67 and 27g_91, respectively. For comparison to CaV1.342 see Fig. 2.

###xml 136 137 136 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>

###xml 173 174 173 174 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 177 185 177 181 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C76</sub>
###xml 250 251 246 247 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 254 263 250 255 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C158</sub>
###xml 276 277 268 269 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 280 288 272 276 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C76</sub>
###xml 328 329 316 317 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 332 334 320 322 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 382 384 370 372 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">76</sub>
###xml 421 422 409 410 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">1</xref>

###xml 904 910 892 898 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6</xref>
###xml 1096 1097 1080 1081 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1100 1109 1084 1089 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C116</sub>

###xml 1250 1251 1230 1231 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1254 1263 1234 1239 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C116</sub>
###xml 1291 1292 1267 1268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1292 1294 1268 1270 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 1299 1300 1275 1276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1300 1302 1276 1278 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 1327 1328 1303 1304 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1331 1334 1307 1310 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 1357 1358 1333 1334 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1361 1369 1337 1341 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#916;C76</sub>
###xml 1421 1422 1393 1394 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1425 1427 1397 1399 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42</sub>
###xml 1460 1463 1432 1435 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">116</sub>
###xml 1473 1479 1445 1451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4</xref>
###xml 1491 1492 1463 1464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">1</xref>
###xml 1494 1495 1466 1467 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">2</xref>
###xml 1497 1498 1469 1470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl3">3</xref>
###xml 1638 1639 1610 1611 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1639 1641 1611 1613 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca</sub>
###xml 1661 1662 1633 1634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 1671 1672 1643 1644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1716 1717 1688 1689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</italic>
###xml 1717 1719 1689 1691 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ba</sub>
###xml 1729 1730 1701 1702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1768 1769 1740 1741 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
To further restrict the protein domain important for CTM activity, we introduced additional truncations in the distal C terminus (Figs. 4, 5, 6). Deletion of the last 76 (CaV1.3DeltaC76) amino acids induced the same gating effects as described for CaV1.3DeltaC158. However, CaV1.3DeltaC76 channel activity was not reverted to CaV1.342-like behavior by co-expression of peptide GFP-C76 (for data and statistics see Tables 1, 2, 3). This could not be explained by a lack of GFP-C76 expression because full-length expression of this peptide was confirmed in Western blot experiments where the peptide expressed at comparable levels to GFP-C158 (n = 3, not illustrated). Our data therefore suggest that the last 76 amino acids are required for the formation of CTM activity but cannot functionally recombine with its truncated counterpart to form a modulatory structure. Sequence alignment with other LTCCs (Fig. 6) revealed that truncation DeltaC76 cuts in half the most distal highly conserved domain. This may prevent recombination to a functional domain upon co-expression. Hence, we generated CaV1.3DeltaC116 in which the conserved region was fully removed and subsequently co-expressed as a single peptide. As shown in Fig. 4 and Tables 1, 2, 3, CaV1.3DeltaC116 again exhibited functional ICa and IBa properties similar to CaV1.342A. However, unlike in CaV1.3DeltaC76, the gating properties were reversed to those of CaV1.342 after co-expression of the GFP-C116 peptide (Fig. 4 and Tables 1, 2, 3). Co-expression of the corresponding distal peptides not only reversed activation parameters and CDI but also significantly decreased mean ICa density by 53-63% (p < 0.05, n = 7-11). A similar trend was also seen for IBa (41-67%, n = 7-11). These data implicate that CaV1.3 alpha1 subunits contain critical structural elements required for CTM function within the last 76 amino acids and that the last 116 residues perform CTM activity when co-expressed in HEK-293 cells.
###end p 62

###xml 1139 1140 1125 1126 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</sub>
###xml 1143 1146 1129 1132 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">42A</sub>
###xml 1170 1173 1156 1159 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">116</sub>
###xml 1196 1197 1182 1183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">h</italic>
